2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

Find Python source files in django/django that implement Django's MIDDLEWARE setting processing: the middleware stack construction, the process_request/process_response calling order, and how Django's middleware compares to WSGI middleware stacking in terms of call order.

272026-03-08T20:02:51.979666agentmessage-
The answer file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json`. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Django Middleware Processing — Key Findings

### Middleware Stack Construction (`load_middleware`)
The core is in **`django/core/handlers/base.py`** — `BaseHandler.load_middleware()`. It iterates `settings.MIDDLEWARE` **in reverse**, wrapping each middleware around the previous handler starting from `_get_response`. The final `_middleware_chain` callable is the outermost middleware (first in `MIDDLEWARE`).

### Call Order
- **`process_request`** (via `MiddlewareMixin.__call__`): called in MIDDLEWARE list order (first → last)
- **`process_response`**: called in reverse order (last → first), because each middleware wraps the next
- **`process_view`**: inserted at index 0 during construction → runs in MIDDLEWARE order
- **`process_template_response`** and **`process_exception`**: appended → run in reverse MIDDLEWARE order

### WSGI Middleware Comparison
Django's chain is structurally identical to WSGI middleware stacking (`mw1(mw2(mw3(app)))`). The key difference from the old `MIDDLEWARE_CLASSES`: under `MIDDLEWARE`, if a middleware short-circuits, only outer layers see the response — matching true WSGI onion semantics. `convert_exception_to_response()` (in `django/core/handlers/exception.py`) wraps each layer to prevent exception leakage between middleware.

### Key Files
- `django/core/handlers/base.py` — `BaseHandler`, `load_middleware`, `_get_response`, `adapt_method_mode`
- `django/core/handlers/exception.py` — `convert_exception_to_response`
- `django/core/handlers/wsgi.py` — `WSGIHandler`
- `django/core/handlers/asgi.py` — `ASGIHandler`
- `django/utils/deprecation.py` — `MiddlewareMixin` (old-style hook compatibility)
- All files in `django/middleware/` and relevant `d
... (truncated)

MIDDLEWARE setting processing is implemented primarily in django/core/handlers/base.py, with supporting infrastructure in django/core/handlers/exception.py, django/core/handlers/wsgi.py, django/core/handlers/asgi.py, and django/utils/deprecation.py.\\n\\n## Middleware Stack Construction (load_middleware)\\n\\nThe central function is `BaseHandler.load_middleware()` in `django/core/handlers/base.py`. It builds the middleware chain by iterating over `settings.MIDDLEWARE` **in reverse order** (line 41: `for middleware_path in reversed(settings.MIDDLEWARE)`). Starting from the innermost handler (`_get_response` or `_get_response_async`), each middleware is instantiated by calling `middleware(adapted_handler)`, wrapping the previous handler. The result is stored in `self._middleware_chain`.\\n\\nDuring construction, `load_middleware` also populates three separate lists:\\n- `_view_middleware`: middleware with `process_view()` hooks (inserted at index 0, so first-listed middleware runs first)\\n- `_template_response_middleware`: middleware with `process_template_response()` hooks (appended, so last-listed middleware runs first on response)\\n- `_exception_middleware`: middleware with `process_exception()` hooks (appended)\\n\\nEach middleware is wrapped with `convert_exception_to_response()` from `django/core/handlers/exception.py`, ensuring no middleware leaks exceptions to the next layer.\\n\\n## process_request / process_response Calling Order\\n\\nDjango's new-style middleware (since Django 1.10) uses a single `__call__(request)` interface. The middleware chain is an onion: the first middleware in `MIDDLEWARE` is the outermost layer. When a request arrives:\\n1. `get_response(request)` calls `self._middleware_chain(request)` \u2014 the outermost middleware.\\n2. Each middleware calls `self.get_response(request)` (the next middleware inward) to get the response.\\n3. The innermost callable is `_get_response()`, which resolves the URL, applies `_view_middleware` (in MIDDLEWARE order), calls the view, applies `_template_response_middleware` (in reverse MIDDLEWARE order), and renders the response.\\n4. On the way back out, each middleware can modify the response.\\n\\nFor old-style middleware using `MiddlewareMixin` (in `django/utils/deprecation.py`), the `__call__` method explicitly calls `self.process_request(request)` before `self.get_response(request)`, and `self.process_response(request, response)` after \u2014 preserving the old-style hook semantics within the new callable interface.\\n\\n## Comparison with WSGI Middleware Stacking\\n\\nDjango's middleware chain is structurally identical to WSGI middleware stacking: each middleware wraps the next application/handler via a callable. In WSGI, middleware is stacked as `mw1(mw2(mw3(app)))`, where `mw1` is outermost. Django's `load_middleware` builds the same structure by iterating `settings.MIDDLEWARE` in reverse and wrapping each successive handler.\\n\\nThe key behavioral difference is that Django's middleware (under the `MIDDLEWARE` setting, not the old `MIDDLEWARE_CLASSES`) behaves like a true onion: if a middleware short-circuits by returning a response early, only that middleware and the ones before it (outer layers) will process the response on the way out. This matches WSGI middleware semantics exactly. Under the old `MIDDLEWARE_CLASSES`, every middleware's `process_response` was always called regardless of short-circuiting.\\n\\n## Key Files\\n\\n- **`django/core/handlers/base.py`**: `BaseHandler` with `load_middleware`, `_get_response`, `_get_response_async`, `get_response`, `get_response_async`, `adapt_method_mode`, `process_exception_by_middleware`, `resolve_request`.\\n- **`django/core/handlers/exception.py`**: `convert_exception_to_response` (wraps each middleware layer in exception handling), `response_for_exception`, `handle_uncaught_exception`.\\n- **`django/core/handlers/wsgi.py`**: `WSGIHandler` (calls `load_middleware()` in `__init__`, implements WSGI `__call__`).\\n- **`django/core/handlers/asgi.py`**: `ASGIHandler` (calls `load_middleware(is_async=True)` in `__init__`).\\n- **`django/utils/deprecation.py`**: `MiddlewareMixin` \u2014 compatibility class that bridges old-style `process_request`/`process_response` hooks into the new callable interface.\\n- **`django/middleware/`**: All built-in middleware implementations (cache, clickjacking, common, csp, csrf, gzip, http, locale, security).\\n- **`django/contrib/auth/middleware.py`**: `AuthenticationMiddleware`, `LoginRequiredMiddleware`, `RemoteUserMiddleware`.\\n- **`django/contrib/sessions/middleware.py`**: `SessionMiddleware`.\\n- **`django/contrib/messages/middleware.py`**: `MessageMiddleware`.\\n- **`django/utils/decorators.py`**: `decorator_from_middleware` utility for applying middleware to individual views.\"\n}\n",
